Gallagher&#160;&amp; Co. (the Company) issued a press release setting forth the Company&#8217;s financial results for the quarter and full year ended December&#160;31, 2020 (the Earnings Release).  </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right"><B>NEWS RELEASE </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>ARTHUR J. GALLAGHER&nbsp;&amp; CO. ANNOUNCES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>FOURTH QUARTER AND FULL YEAR 2020 FINANCIAL RESULTS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">ROLLING MEADOWS, IL, January&nbsp;28, 2021 &#151; Arthur J. Gallagher&nbsp;&amp; Co. (NYSE: AJG) today reported its financial results for the quarter and year
ended December&nbsp;31, 2020. Management will host a webcast conference call to discuss these results on Thursday, January&nbsp;28, 2021 at 5:15 p.m. ET/4:15 p.m. CT. To listen to the call, and for printer-friendly formats of this release and the
&#147;Supplemental Quarterly Data&#148; and &#147;CFO Commentary,&#148; which may also be referenced during the call, please visit <U>ajg.com/IR</U>. These documents contain both GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures.
Investors and other users of this information should read carefully the section entitled &#147;Information Regarding <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Measures&#148; beginning on page&nbsp;10. </P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We delivered another excellent quarter, and a fantastic full year during which we generated record
profits,&#148; said J.&nbsp;Patrick Gallagher, Jr., Chairman, President and CEO. &#147;Despite the pandemic and the resulting economic fall out, we executed on our long-term operating priorities: growing both organically and through acquisitions,
improving both our productivity and quality, and still investing in our bedrock culture. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We are operating in a property casualty environment where
rates are up around 8% globally, terms and conditions are tightening, and capacity in certain lines is increasingly constrained. We see these market conditions continuing in 2021. In addition, we are seeing increased business activity, a recovering
labor market, and a rebound in new arising risk management claims. An environment of rising rates and growing exposure units provides a near-perfect opportunity for us to demonstrate that we provide the very best insurance, consulting and risk
management advice for our clients. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;I would like to thank all Gallagher professionals around the globe for being flexible, working hard and never
losing focus on delivering outstanding client service. I am extremely proud of our collective successes during 2020, especially how we came together to work as a team, even while physically apart. Our performance in 2020, more than ever, represents
The Gallagher Way!&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Summary of Financial Results &#150; Year Ended December&nbsp;31, </B></P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2020, the pretax impact of the Brokerage segment adjustments totals
$125.8&nbsp;million, with a corresponding adjustment to the provision for income taxes of $28.1&nbsp;million relating to these items. For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2020, the pretax impact of the Risk Management segment adjustments totals
$8.5&nbsp;million, with a corresponding adjustment to the provision for income taxes of $2.1&nbsp;million relating to these items. There is no pretax impact of the Corporate segment adjustments, but there is an adjustment to the provision for income
taxes of $1.1&nbsp;million relating to the tax item noted on page&nbsp;8. A detailed reconciliation of the 2020 and 2019 provision (benefit) for income taxes is shown on pages&nbsp;14 and 15. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">(2 of 15) </P>

</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> Impact </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In our property/casualty Brokerage operations, during fourth quarter 2020, (a) our customer retention remained at
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, (b)&nbsp;new business generation was above <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, offset somewhat by <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-recurring</FONT> business
that was below <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, (c)&nbsp;renewal exposure units (i.e., insured values, payrolls, employees, miles driven, etc.) declined; however, premium rates across most geographies and lines of
coverage have continued to increase, effectively mitigating exposure unit declines, and (d)&nbsp;net positive <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-term</FONT> policy modifications were slightly higher than fourth quarter 2019. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Thus far in the first quarter of 2021, property/casualty customer exposure unit renewals showed improvement compared to lows seen in April and May 2020, as
our customers&#146; businesses continue to recover and economic activity increases. Full policy cancellations have remained similar to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, and we continue to see property/casualty premium
rates move higher overall which may partially, or fully, offset future declines in exposure units, if any. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In our employee benefits Brokerage operations,
during the fourth quarter of 2020 we saw a decrease in new consulting and special project work, while covered lives on renewal business were similar to the third quarter of 2020. Our January&nbsp;1, 2021 health and welfare renewals have shown
covered lives being consistent with levels seen in the fourth quarter of 2020, although still not at <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels. Consulting engagements and special project work improved slightly from fourth quarter
levels, but are still below <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels. We believe revenue softness related to reduced covered lives and lower frequency of special project work could persist over the next few quarters, and even
deteriorate further, if the economy is slow to recover. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In our Risk Management operations, we began seeing a meaningful decline in new claims arising
during the last two weeks of March 2020, which persisted into April. From May to December 2020, we saw an improving trend in new claims arising and higher COVID-related workers compensation claims; yet the current level of weekly new claims so far
in 2021 is still below <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels. A slower recovery or reversal in the number of workers employed could cause fewer claims to arise in future quarters. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Throughout 2020 and in the fourth quarter of 2020, our clean energy investments experienced the impact of lower electricity consumption in the U.S., when
compared to the same periods in 2019, due to reduced economic activity (as well as, unrelated to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19,</FONT> milder temperatures, other than some brief periods of unusually warm weather, falling natural gas
prices, and increased use of renewable energy sources). We expect reduced U.S. electricity consumption could persist at least through the first half of 2021, and could even continue throughout all of 2021. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Of our nearly 1,000 office locations, nearly 400 are open, but most at reduced capacity. Accordingly the vast majority of our employees continue to work
remotely for some or all of their work week. We believe our service levels are unchanged from <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels. We have not had any office-wide outbreaks of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19,</FONT>
and fewer than 300 confirmed cases among our 32,400 employees - all of which we believe contracted the virus outside of our office locations. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Given the
deterioration in economic conditions since the first quarter of 2020, we are actively managing costs by limiting discretionary spending such as travel, entertainment and advertising expenses, adjusting our real estate footprint, reducing capital
expenditures, limiting use of outside labor and consultants, increasing utilization of our centers of excellence, and we have adjusted portions of our workforce where volumes have declined significantly and normal attrition was not sufficient. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The cost saving impact of these actions in the second, third and fourth quarters of 2020 was substantial; with estimated quarterly savings of approximately
$65&nbsp;million to $70&nbsp;million pretax compared to the same quarters in 2019, as adjusted for pro forma full-quarter costs related to acquisitions. Offsetting these savings were severance and lease termination costs related to these actions. We
believe savings in the first quarter of 2021 compared to the first quarter of 2020 could again total approximately $60&nbsp;million to $65&nbsp;million pretax after adjusting for pro forma costs related to acquisitions. Offsetting possible future
savings would be additional implementation and execution costs, which we estimate could total approximately $5&nbsp;million to $10&nbsp;million pretax. Future net savings may be lower if the economy recovers faster than we are forecasting or our
costs to implement changes exceed our estimates. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We have not seen any meaningful decline in cash receipts from our clients to date and we have more than
$1.6&nbsp;billion of available liquidity. A prolonged period of economic weakness may cause future cash collections to deteriorate, but we believe our cost savings, reduced <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-client</FONT> facing capital
expenditures and working capital improvements could mitigate a potential decline in our cash flows over the near-term. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">(3 of 15) </P>

</DIV></Center>

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(4)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">During third quarter 2019, Gallagher and/or our 46.5% owned affiliate, Chem-Mod LLC, incurred costs related to
(a)&nbsp;settling certain litigation, (b)&nbsp;prevailing in a tax court matter, (c)&nbsp;defending a new patent matter, and (d)&nbsp;moving three 2011 Era plants into different locations that generated more
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> earnings in 2020 than in 2019. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Interest and banking costs and</B> <B>debt </B>- At
December&nbsp;31, 2020, Gallagher had $4,348.0&nbsp;million of borrowings from private placements, no short-term borrowings under its line of credit facility and $203.6&nbsp;million outstanding under a revolving loan facility that provides funding
for premium finance receivables, which are fully collateralized by the underlying premiums held by insurance carriers, and as such are excluded from our debt covenant computations. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Clean energy -</B> Consists of the operating results related to our investments in 21 active clean coal production plants in 2020 (34 in 2019 and prior
years) and royalty income from clean coal licenses related to Chem-Mod LLC. Additional information regarding these results is available in the &#147;CFO Commentary&#148; <U>at ajg.com/IR</U>. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Acquisition costs -</B> Consists mostly of external professional fees and other due diligence costs related to acquisitions. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Corporate </B>-<B> </B>Consists of overhead allocations mostly related to corporate staff compensation and other corporate level activities. In addition,
this includes the tax expense related to the impact of the U.S. tax legislation passed in December 2017 - principally the partial taxation of foreign earnings, nondeductible executive compensation and entertainment expenses. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Income Taxes </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gallagher allocates the provision for
income taxes to its Brokerage and Risk Management segments using the local country statutory rates. Gallagher&#146;s consolidated effective tax rate for the quarters ended December&nbsp;31, 2020 and 2019 was (14.5)% and (25.7)%, respectively, which
was lower than the statutory rate due to the amount of IRC Section&nbsp;45 tax credits. In third quarter 2020, Gallagher increased its estimated U.K. effective income tax rate from 17.5% to 19%. In fourth quarter 2019, Gallagher lowered its
estimated U.S. effective income tax rate from 26% to 25%. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Webcast Conference Call </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gallagher will host a webcast conference call on Thursday, January&nbsp;28, 2021 at 5:15 p.m. ET/4:15 p.m. CT. To listen to this call, please go to
<U>ajg.com/IR</U>. The call will be available for replay at such website for at least 90 days. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Arthur J. Gallagher&nbsp;&amp; Co. </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Arthur J. Gallagher&nbsp;&amp; Co., an international insurance brokerage and risk management services firm, is headquartered in Rolling Meadows, Illinois, has
operations in 49 countries and offers client-service capabilities in more than 150 countries around the world through a network of correspondent brokers and consultants. </P>

of forward-looking statements include, but are not limited to, statements regarding (i)&nbsp;future actions the Company may take in response to the disruption caused by <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19;</FONT> (ii) anticipated future
results or performance of any segment or the Company as a whole; (iii)&nbsp;the premium rate environment and the state of insurance markets; and (iv)&nbsp;the economic environment. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gallagher&#146;s actual results may differ materially from those contemplated by the forward-looking statements. Readers are therefore cautioned against

our services; our ability to sell and provide our services, including limitations on travel and difficulties of our clients and employees working from home and closure of their facilities; the ability of our clients to pay their insurance premiums
which could impact our commission and fee revenues for our services; the nature and extent of possible claims that might impact the ability of underwriting enterprises to pay supplemental and contingent commissions; the decrease in new arising
workers&#146; compensation and general liability claims; the long-term impact of closing our offices and our employees working from home; the impact of lost revenue on our employees&#146; variable and base compensation levels; the impact of reduced
investments and postponements related to business modernization projects; the impact of furloughed or terminated employees; and the impact of reduced advertising and sponsorship investments. </P>

included herein or the corresponding earnings release posted on Gallagher&#146;s website. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Information Regarding
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Measures </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In addition to reporting financial results in accordance with GAAP, this press release
provides information regarding EBITDAC, EBITDAC margin, adjusted EBITDAC, adjusted EBITDAC margin, diluted net earnings per share, as adjusted (adjusted EPS), adjusted revenue, adjusted compensation and operating expenses, adjusted compensation
expense ratio, adjusted operating expense ratio and organic revenue.&nbsp;These measures are not in accordance with, or an alternative to, the GAAP information provided in this press release.&nbsp;Gallagher&#146;s management believes that these
presentations provide useful information to management, analysts and investors regarding financial and business trends relating to Gallagher&#146;s results of operations and financial condition or because they provide investors with measures that
our chief operating decision maker uses when reviewing the company&#146;s performance. See further below for definitions and additional reasons each of these measures is useful to investors. Gallagher&#146;s industry peers may provide similar
supplemental <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> information with respect to one or more of these measures, although they may not use the same or comparable terminology and may not make identical adjustments.&nbsp;The <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> information provided by Gallagher should be used in addition to, but not as a substitute for, the GAAP information provided.&nbsp;As disclosed in its most recent Proxy Statement, Gallagher makes
determinations regarding certain elements of executive officer incentive compensation, performance share awards and annual cash incentive awards, partly on the basis of measures related to adjusted EBITDAC. Certain reclassifications have been made
to the prior year amounts reported in this press release in order to conform them to the current year presentation. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Adjusted <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> presentation</B> - Gallagher believes that the adjusted <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> presentations of the current and prior period information presented in this earnings release provide
stockholders and other interested persons with useful information regarding certain financial metrics of Gallagher that may assist such persons in analyzing Gallagher&#146;s operating results as they develop a future earnings outlook for Gallagher.
The <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> amounts related to the adjustments were computed using the normalized effective tax rate for each respective period. See pages&nbsp;14 and 15 for a reconciliation of the adjustments made to
income taxes. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Earnings Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>EBITDAC</B> <B>and EBITDAC margin </B>- EBITDAC is net earnings before interest, income taxes, depreciation,
amortization and the change in estimated acquisition earnout payables and EBITDAC margin is EBITDAC divided by total revenues (for the Brokerage segment) and revenues before reimbursements (for the Risk Management segment). These measures for the
Brokerage and Risk Management segments provide a meaningful representation of Gallagher&#146;s operating performance for the overall business and provide a meaningful way to measure its financial performance on an ongoing basis.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EBITDAC</B> <B>and Adjusted EBITDAC Margin </B>- Adjusted EBITDAC is EBITDAC adjusted to exclude net
gains on divestitures, acquisition integration costs, workforce related charges, lease termination related charges, acquisition related adjustments and the period-over-period impact of foreign currency translation, as applicable and Adjusted EBITDAC
margin is Adjusted EBITDAC divided by total adjusted revenues (defined above). These measures for the Brokerage and Risk Management segments provide a meaningful representation of Gallagher&#146;s operating performance, and are also presented to
improve the comparability of our results between periods by eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of variability. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EPS and Adjusted Net Earnings </B>- Adjusted net earnings have been adjusted to exclude the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> impact of net gains on divestitures, acquisition integration costs, the impact of foreign currency translation, workforce related charges, lease termination related charges, acquisition related adjustments
and effective income tax rate impact, as applicable. Adjusted EPS is Adjusted Net Earnings divided by diluted weighted average shares outstanding. This measure provides a meaningful representation of Gallagher&#146;s operating performance (and as
such should not be used as a measure of Gallagher&#146;s liquidity), and for the overall business is also presented to improve the comparability of our results between periods by eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of
variability. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Organic Revenues (a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure)</B> - For the Brokerage segment, organic
change in base commission and fee revenues, supplemental revenues and contingent revenues exclude the first twelve months of such revenues generated from acquisitions and such revenues related to divested operations and program repricing in each
year presented.&nbsp;These revenues are excluded from organic revenues in order to help interested persons analyze the revenue growth associated with the operations that were a part of Gallagher in both the current and prior periods.&nbsp;In
addition, organic change in base commission and fee revenues, supplemental revenues and contingent revenues excludes the period-over-period impact of foreign currency translation. For the Risk Management segment, organic change in fee revenues
excludes the first twelve months of fee revenues generated from acquisitions and the fee revenues related to operations disposed of in each year presented. In addition, change in organic growth excludes the period-over-period impact of foreign
currency translation to improve the comparability of our results between periods by eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of variability or are due to the limited-time nature of these revenue sources. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">These revenue items are excluded from organic revenues in order to determine a comparable, but <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP,</FONT> measurement
of revenue growth that is associated with the revenue sources that are expected to continue in the current year and beyond.&nbsp;Gallagher has historically viewed organic revenue growth as an important indicator when assessing and evaluating the
performance of its Brokerage and Risk Management segments.&nbsp;Gallagher also believes that using this <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure allows readers of our financial statements to measure, analyze and compare the growth
from its Brokerage and Risk Management segments in a meaningful and consistent manner. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Reconciliation of
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Information Presented to GAAP Measures</B> - This press release includes tabular reconciliations to the most comparable GAAP measures, as follows: for EBITDAC (on pages&nbsp;12 and 13), for adjusted
revenues, adjusted EBITDAC and adjusted diluted net earnings per share (on pages&nbsp;1 and 2), for organic revenue measures (on pages&nbsp;4 and 6, respectively, for the Brokerage and Risk Management segments), for adjusted compensation and
operating expenses and adjusted EBITDAC margin (on pages&nbsp;5, 6 and 7, respectively, for the Brokerage and Risk Management segments). </P>
